<div id="review_361823206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361823206" />
    <a title="Ralph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/692779-ralph"><img alt="Ralph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219697396p2/692779.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361823206?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ralph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ralph" href="/user/show/692779-ralph">Ralph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361823206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer240865110466275821">I picked this up from the dreaded "Popular Library" section of the LA Library, where I go when I am returning a book and am too lazy to go up to the stacks to look for something. I'm left to judge books by their covers, or in this case, by the name of author. Of course every book has some advanced praise for their author by some other authors you haven't heard of. Same here. But I figured if Steve Martin isn't a bad writer (note Steve Martin did not give any advanced praise to Franco, just namin</span>
  <span id="freeText240865110466275821" style="display:none">I picked this up from the dreaded "Popular Library" section of the LA Library, where I go when I am returning a book and am too lazy to go up to the stacks to look for something. I'm left to judge books by their covers, or in this case, by the name of author. Of course every book has some advanced praise for their author by some other authors you haven't heard of. Same here. But I figured if Steve Martin isn't a bad writer (note Steve Martin did not give any advanced praise to Franco, just naming an actor who is a passable writer), maybe James Franco might have something to say. <br /><br />Half way through, I am convinced James Franco is an idiot. It is obvious that no one was willing to tell him, no, you are not a Renaissance man. You are not smart enough. Not just not smart enough, not sensitive or artistic enough. If there were a Razzies for books, this would win. If he were not a celebrity, this book of short stories would not be published. This book is truly, heartwrenching-ly stupid. Is he doing a Joachim Phoenix and tricking people into thinking he is delusional, when he is purposely awful? No, I don't see it. My God, this makes me want to run to the library right now to return this book. I truly pity anyone who purchased it. <br /><br />I finished it for the purpose of being a completist. The flaws are many.<br /><br />1. No character development. <br />2. Lack of structure.<br />3. Lack of imagery.<br />4. Lack of plot.<br />5. Multiple first person POV sounds the same for each character.<br />6. Just bad, bad writing. High school kids write better than this.<br /><br />The only bright side is it is short. There's a reference early on to Fast Times at Ridgemont High. I suspect Franco wanted to write a bunch of short stories that paralleled Fast Times but he just didn't have a single good story to tell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="240865110466275821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135315938?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Glover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Glover" href="/user/show/650912-maggie-glover">Maggie Glover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135315938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16883053614890053857">If you know me, then you probably know I love James Franco. I loved James Franco before it was cool to love James Franco (and certainly before it was not cool to love James Franco). Admittedly, if this book wasn't by James Franco, I probably wouldn't have read it. More importantly, it probably wouldn't have been published. As a writer struggling to get her first book published, I'm one of the first to voice frustration when a celebrity like Franco (or Jewel...) get a book published just because </span>
  <span id="freeText16883053614890053857" style="display:none">If you know me, then you probably know I love James Franco. I loved James Franco before it was cool to love James Franco (and certainly before it was not cool to love James Franco). Admittedly, if this book wasn't by James Franco, I probably wouldn't have read it. More importantly, it probably wouldn't have been published. As a writer struggling to get her first book published, I'm one of the first to voice frustration when a celebrity like Franco (or Jewel...) get a book published just because of their name. However, I believe that their fame can also be a curse, since their work gets published without ever getting any "real" feedback, or suffering the many, many rejections that most of us writers are used to. Therefore, their work doesn't get a chance to finish "cooking" before it's thrust before the judgment of the public.<br /><br />Which brings me to my point: this book reminded me of a portfolio of work from a talented creative writing student with a lot of potential. There were some fresh and resonating images, a smattering of interesting, round characters and some stories that really stayed with me. There were also some cliched characters, some gratuitous (seemingly for shock value) violence and, as other reviewers have stated, definitely some repetition in plot. If James Franco wasn't a celebrity, he probably would have spent a few more years (or decades) working on new material. But, because he is who he is, he published the first collection of stories that he pulled together. Unfortunately, the lack of experience shows in this work.<br /><br />I still love him though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16883053614890053857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14404014882712174879">Can I give this less than one star? It is possibly the most boring, ill-written fiction I've ever read; every story is the same, every character is the same. It's impossible to tell the stories apart, and the plot is non-existent. <br/><br/>The few page stories feature two types of people.. An angsty, misunderstood, know-it-all, teenage boy, or a ''slutty'' teenage girl who enjoys being raped by older men and smoking. Every one of them is a homophobic, egotistical, racist, arrogant asshole.<br/><br/>It reads like i</span>
  <span id="freeText14404014882712174879" style="display:none">Can I give this less than one star? It is possibly the most boring, ill-written fiction I've ever read; every story is the same, every character is the same. It's impossible to tell the stories apart, and the plot is non-existent. <br /><br />The few page stories feature two types of people.. An angsty, misunderstood, know-it-all, teenage boy, or a ''slutty'' teenage girl who enjoys being raped by older men and smoking. Every one of them is a homophobic, egotistical, racist, arrogant asshole.<br /><br />It reads like it's been written by someone trying way too hard to be deep and artistic, when in reality there is no substance or meaning behind anything. It's there for purely vanity reasons.<br /><br />Seriously, don't waste your time or money.</span>

  <span id="freeText1109003417218172370" style="display:none"><b> 0 stars </b> <br><br><b> <u> Fair warning </u></b> , this is going to be more of a rant, than a review. To give you the indication of how I felt during the book this is a direct quote of a message I sent to a friend <i> Palo alto..what the fuck! I wish i was able to be a "dnf" kinda person</i>. Sadly for me I cannot leave books unfinished so onward I read, and in my own words <i> If i made it through Karenina I can do this </i>.<br><br>So pray tell why did I not enjoy the "literary works" of Mr Franco? Was it his <b> terrible </b> writing? (some would say this was intentional due to the teenage theme and hearing "their voice"), was it the abrupt ending of stories which left you thinking <i> wtf was the point in that </i>? was it the same themes repeating over and over and over again?, was it the fucked-up mentalities of the characters?....no friends it was all of these things. <br><br>I think this best describes James Franco's "inspiration" for this book...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432639727ra/14992629.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>Favourite short stories you might ask? Opening line of the book <i> Ten years ago, my sophomore year in high school, I killed a woman on Halloween </i> Reading this you might think it will be a story of redemption, alas it is not. The main character was drunk, upset over a girl and flying through the streets <i> the figure was lying facedown on the road. There was no one else around....I took the moment and drove off, before she started moving...I never told anyone about the accident. </i> A few years later he goes past the scene and his only thought is <i> Oh yeah, that’s where the accident happened </i><br>Thanks Franco, where will the book go next... <br><br>Moving onto the next story, this one told from the perspective of a quiet nerd. She goes to a house party, there are delinquent kids, she talks to boy, boy gets in fight out the front and gets run over <i><br>Everyone scrambled and dove out of the way, and the SUV drove over Ronny’s body. </i> At least we got a great description of the victim <i> Ronny’s face was smashed on one side, and swollen like a white balloon on the other. </i> but don't you worry <i> Nobody did anything until the police arrived </i><br> <i> Ronny died. I didn’t get invited to the funeral. </i><br>Good thing the story was all about this poor girl. <br><br>Now I could go into why I disliked all the other stories however I have more reviews to write, and actual books I want to read. It would however be remiss of me not to talk <b> Chinatown </b> <br>Now this was a great story...girl moves to town, girl meets main character Roberto who within hours has sex with her, or as he so eloquently puts it <i> I spit on my hand, and then I put my dick inside her </i>. If that wasn't good enough Roberto and his mates then all go to the park with the girl who <i> stayed on her knees </i> whilst each one of them steps up for a blow job. From here the story just gets worse and worse and we find the girl at a house party where <i> everyone fucked her </i>. Now the girl Pam isn't innocent in all of this however it was still a horrible story to read. And the story showed that essentially Franco is fucked up. <i> I put a cucumber inside her. She didn’t really want it, but I shoved it up there. I kept it up there for a while </i>. The end of the story we see that the cops have been called, however there was nothing they can do and Franco wraps the story up with some wonderful prose <i> when we got older, I did things in my life and she did things in her life </i> <br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>So would I have rated this "book" lower if I could. Yes. A million times yes. <br>Stick to your acting Franco, ain't no one got time for this shit. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432639727ra/14992630.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_618861223" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618861223" />
    <a title="Ashleigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3507002-ashleigh"><img alt="Ashleigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521917757p2/3507002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618861223?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleigh" href="/user/show/3507002-ashleigh">Ashleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780571273164" href="/book/show/10285469-palo-alto">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3507002-ashleigh?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3507002-ashleigh?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3507002-ashleigh?shelf=worst-books">worst-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618861223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1469131022755102799">Well, having read James Franco's opinion on a few things and his involvement in some creative projects and films I thought I could rely on him to produce writing of a tolerable standard. How wrong I was. This book is a joke. His writing is appalling for someone who has so dedicated his studies to English and creative writing. It feels like something I could have written at the age of 11.<br/>He confuses me greatly because even as I type this I am wondering was that the point all along? Did he want to</span>
  <span id="freeText1469131022755102799" style="display:none">Well, having read James Franco's opinion on a few things and his involvement in some creative projects and films I thought I could rely on him to produce writing of a tolerable standard. How wrong I was. This book is a joke. His writing is appalling for someone who has so dedicated his studies to English and creative writing. It feels like something I could have written at the age of 11.<br />He confuses me greatly because even as I type this I am wondering was that the point all along? Did he want to appear juvenile in his authorship? <br />His writing, for a start is all written in the first person, so already he has stripped back much of the depth that can be created. His characters are nothing short of moronic. They have so little depth and everything they say is shallow drivel. Basically they are all pretty much unrealistic and unrelatable. His stories consist of "he went there. I did this." Its pretty boring. <br />Is he making a statement about youth culture? is he trying to be akin to Harmony Korine or Catherine Hardwicke? Even if he is attempting this he completely missed the point. I disagree with the comments saying his work is rascist/homophobic/sexist because at the end of the day he clearly wrote about personal experiences. Is he supposed to pretend there are no rascists/homophobes/sexists just because you dislike them? no. That would be silly. I will however berate him for using these themes as a means to shock people into thinking he has some "new, fresh voice that needs to be heard." His voice says little to nothing 99% of the time anyway so I don't think people should care that much.<br />The chapters are all written from a different characters perspective but his writing style stays the same, there are literally no personal inflections or observations that can allow the reader to differentiate between the characters telling their story which is just plain infuriating. <br />Overall his writing is simple and drab, towards the end of the book he suddenly starts adding the odd paragraph that seem to mean more than the rest, they have some pretty wording and if he had of written the entire thing like this the book would feel a lot more interesting. Those paragraphs though, only add up to a total of 5 or 6 at most. The rest is sadly, rubbish. Save yourself the trouble and miss out this try hard, wannabe pretentious crapfest and read something amazing instead. There is plenty out there and maybe James should have done that too instead of wasting his time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1469131022755102799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1373016259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1373016259" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1439856-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442653009p2/1439856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1373016259?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/1439856-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476778389" href="/book/show/20523860-palo-alto">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1373016259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14212731530367332223">I'm going to have to come to the conclusion, at least based on these stories, that some of the vitriol I've heard directed towards Franco's writing is more due to the chances he gets that other writers do not. I mean, this isn't great writing, but it isn't bad by any means. It is actually pretty solid. It hit some off notes for me, sometimes tries to invoke more grit than I feel it can support, and doesn't always persuade me of the things it seems to think about itself, but it's still actually s</span>
  <span id="freeText14212731530367332223" style="display:none">I'm going to have to come to the conclusion, at least based on these stories, that some of the vitriol I've heard directed towards Franco's writing is more due to the chances he gets that other writers do not. I mean, this isn't great writing, but it isn't bad by any means. It is actually pretty solid. It hit some off notes for me, sometimes tries to invoke more grit than I feel it can support, and doesn't always persuade me of the things it seems to think about itself, but it's still actually some pretty decent writing. That just means it has some rough edges, which perhaps means that Franco isn't as good a writer as he someday could be (in my view). That doesn't make it awful. I think the treatment I've often seen of it comes more from some people saying even nicer things about it than it deserves just based on who Franco is and the fact that someone other than Franco probably wouldn't have gotten the same kind of attention for these kind of stories. I still would have read them and enjoyed them. They aren't perfect, but I certainly didn't find them to be garbage. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14212731530367332223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_18108757'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18108757-it"><img alt="It" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1371855166l/18108757._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DazYPm6N6eFUOzswpp0aVqv4vmjyf5Gk78+Xdpb8ampuqpuw3Z83qk/Bp8paaeD7J4NOBxYffqjppxm+/t44Pg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

In The End of Food, Paul Roberts investigates this system and presents a startling truth—how we make, market, and transport our food is no longer compatible with the billions of consumers the system was built to serve.\n\nThe emergence of large-scale and efficient food production forever changed our relationship with food and ultimately left a vulnerable and paradoxical system in place. High-volume factory systems create new risks for food-borne illness; high-yield crops generate grain, produce, and meat of declining nutritional quality; and while nearly a billion people are overweight, roughly as many people are starving. A synthesis of ethnographic theory and psychoanalytic revelation, where the line between researcher and subject is <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16647903556036700011\" style=\"display:none\">Jeanne Favret-Saada is arguably one of France’s most brilliant anthropologists, and The Anti-Witch is nothing less than a masterpiece. A synthesis of ethnographic theory and psychoanalytic revelation, where the line between researcher and subject is blurred—if not erased—The Anti-Witch develops the contours of an anthropology of therapy, while deeply engaging with what it means to be caught in the logic of witchcraft. Through an intimate and provocative sharing of the ethnographic voice with Madame Flora, a “dewitcher,” Favret-Saada delivers a critical challenge to some of anthropology’s fundamental concepts.\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3369521.James_Franco">About James Franco</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15188022924471910943">James Edward Franco is an American actor, film director, screenwriter, film producer, author, and painter. He began acting during the late 1990s, appearing on the short-lived television series <i>Freaks and Geeks</i> and starring in several teen films. In 2001 he played the title role in Mark Rydell's television biographical film <i>James Dean</i>, which earned him a Golden Globe for Best Actor in a Miniseries </span>
  <span id="freeText15188022924471910943" style="display:none">James Edward Franco is an American actor, film director, screenwriter, film producer, author, and painter. He began acting during the late 1990s, appearing on the short-lived television series <i>Freaks and Geeks</i> and starring in several teen films. In 2001 he played the title role in Mark Rydell's television biographical film <i>James Dean</i>, which earned him a Golden Globe for Best Actor in a Miniseries or Television Film.<br /><br />Franco achieved international fame with his portrayal of Harry Osborn in the <i>Spider-Man</i> trilogy. Since then, his films have included the war film <i>The Great Raid</i> (2005), the 2006 romantic drama <i>Tristan &amp; Isolde</i>, and Justin Lin's drama <i>Annapolis</i> (2006). In 2008, Franco starred in the comedy stoner film <i>Pineapple Express</i> and received a Golden Globe Award nomination for Best Actor in a Motion Picture Musical or Comedy. He played a prominent role in the 2008 biographical film <i>Milk</i>. In 2010, he played the lead role in <i>Howl</i> as Allen Ginsberg, and <i>127 Hours</i>, a film about Aron Ralston, an American mountaineer who cut off his own arm to free himself after he was trapped beneath a boulder. He was nominated for a Golden Globe for his performance.<br /><br />In 2010, Franco published a collection of short stories called <i>Palo Alto.</i> The book is named after the California city where Franco grew up and is dedicated to many of the writers he worked with at Brooklyn College. The book has received mixed reviews; <i>Los Angeles Times</i> called it "the work of an ambitious young man who clearly loves to read, who has a good eye for detail, but who has spent way too much time on style and virtually none on substance". <i>The Guardian</i> said that "The Hollywood star's foray into the literary world may be met with cynicism in some quarters, but this is a promising debut from a most unlikely source."</span>
  <a data-text-id="15188022924471910943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
